# =====================================================
# FILE : 01_WORLD\CALM_BELT.md
# =====================================================

# CALM_BELT

---

# Purpose

`CALM_BELT.md` defines the simulation rules governing the Calm Belt.

The Calm Belt is one of the world's most dangerous maritime regions.

It functions as a natural barrier separating the Four Blues from the Grand Line while creating significant navigational, ecological, and strategic challenges.

This document establishes the environmental rules required for accurate world simulation.

---

# Scope

This document defines:

- Calm Belt Characteristics
- Ocean Behavior
- Navigation Restrictions
- Sea King Habitat
- Environmental Hazards
- Travel Limitations
- Strategic Influence

This document does not define:

- Individual Sea Kings
- Combat Rules
- Ship Systems
- Navigation Equipment
- Weather Mechanics

Those systems are defined in their respective documents.

---

# Core Principle

The Calm Belt is naturally hostile to conventional navigation.

Its danger comes from environmental conditions rather than constant combat.

Crossing the Calm Belt is possible only through exceptional preparation, specialized technology, or extraordinary capability.

---

# Environmental Identity

The Calm Belt is characterized by:

- Almost complete absence of natural wind
- Extremely weak ocean currents
- Unusually calm surface conditions
- Dense Sea King populations
- Limited maritime traffic

These conditions remain persistent throughout the region.

---

# Wind Conditions

Natural wind is nearly nonexistent.

Sailing vessels relying solely on wind propulsion become largely immobile.

Alternative propulsion methods may be required.

Detailed ship mechanics are defined in SHIPS.md.

---

# Ocean Currents

Ocean currents are minimal.

Ships cannot rely on natural current flow for navigation.

Movement becomes significantly slower without active propulsion.

---

# Sea King Habitat

The Calm Belt is the primary habitat of Sea Kings.

Sea King encounters are considered an inherent environmental risk.

Encounter probability depends on factors such as:

- Noise
- Ship size
- Environmental disturbance
- Local ecosystem

Sea King behavior is determined by future creature systems.

---

# Navigation Difficulty

Navigation within the Calm Belt is inherently dangerous.

Potential challenges include:

- Loss of mobility
- Limited escape options
- Reduced maneuverability
- Increased exposure to Sea Kings
- Isolation from trade routes

Navigation systems must respect these limitations.

---

# Travel Risk

Travel through the Calm Belt always involves elevated risk.

Potential outcomes include:

- Delayed travel
- Ship damage
- Resource depletion
- Crew fatigue
- Sea King encounters
- Emergency course changes

Safe passage should never be assumed.

---

# Strategic Importance

Despite its dangers, the Calm Belt possesses significant strategic value.

Possible uses include:

- Concealed travel
- Military operations
- Scientific research
- Rare resource exploration
- Hidden facilities

Strategic activity should remain uncommon due to inherent risk.

---

# Economic Influence

The Calm Belt limits commercial transportation.

Trade routes naturally avoid the region whenever possible.

Crossing costs are significantly higher than conventional routes.

Economic simulations should reflect these logistical challenges.

---

# Ecological Balance

The Calm Belt functions as a unique ecosystem.

Its biological diversity differs significantly from surrounding seas.

Large marine life dominates the region.

Environmental disturbances may temporarily alter local ecological behavior.

---

# Accessibility

The Calm Belt is not completely inaccessible.

However,

successful entry and exit require exceptional circumstances.

The AI Game Master should evaluate access based on:

- Ship capability
- Crew experience
- Navigation systems
- Environmental conditions
- Current world state

---

# World Simulation

The Calm Belt continues evolving independently.

Possible ongoing developments include:

- Sea King migration
- Ecological changes
- Hidden discoveries
- Scientific expeditions
- Military observation
- Illegal operations

Simulation continues regardless of player presence.

---

# AI Game Master Responsibilities

The AI must:

- Preserve environmental tension.
- Respect natural navigation limitations.
- Simulate realistic ecological behavior.
- Maintain consistent Sea King presence.
- Apply identical environmental rules to all characters.

The AI must never:

- Treat the Calm Belt as ordinary ocean.
- Ignore navigation penalties.
- Eliminate environmental danger without justification.
- Allow effortless crossing.

---

# Integration

Parent Documents:

- WORLD.md
- TIMELINE.md
- SEAS.md

Related Documents:

- GRAND_LINE.md
- RED_LINE.md
- NAVIGATION.md
- WEATHER.md
- WORLD_EVENTS.md

Integrated Systems:

- SHIPS.md
- DICE.md
- COMBAT.md
- MEDICAL.md
- SAVE_FORMAT.md

---

# Design Principles

The Calm Belt exists to create meaningful geographical limitations.

Risk creates preparation.

Preparation creates strategy.

Strategy creates meaningful exploration.

---

# Source of Truth

`CALM_BELT.md`

is the authoritative specification governing all simulation rules related to the Calm Belt.

All future systems involving navigation, environmental hazards, ecology, and strategic movement within the Calm Belt must follow the rules defined in this document.

# =====================================================
# FILE : 01_WORLD\GRAND_LINE.md
# =====================================================

# GRAND_LINE

---

# Purpose

`GRAND_LINE.md` defines the simulation rules governing the Grand Line.

The Grand Line is the most dangerous and unpredictable maritime region in the world.

Unlike the Four Blues, navigation within the Grand Line follows unique natural laws that significantly affect exploration, travel, combat, logistics, and survival.

This document establishes the rules required for consistent world simulation.

---

# Scope

This document defines:

- Grand Line Environment
- Navigation Rules
- Ocean Characteristics
- Climate Instability
- Travel Conditions
- Regional Simulation
- Environmental Hazards

This document does not define:

- Individual Islands
- Island Weather
- Sea Kings
- Calm Belt
- Red Line

Those systems are defined in their respective documents.

---

# Core Principle

The Grand Line rejects predictability.

Natural laws behave differently from the Four Blues.

Success depends on preparation rather than luck.

Every voyage carries inherent risk.

---

# Geographic Definition

The Grand Line is a continuous ocean belt encircling the world.

It is separated from the Four Blues by the Red Line and the Calm Belt.

Entry into the Grand Line is limited by geography and environmental conditions.

Travel routes are naturally constrained.

---

# Environmental Identity

The Grand Line is characterized by:

- Unstable weather
- Rapid climate shifts
- Irregular sea currents
- Abnormal magnetic fields
- Dangerous wildlife
- Difficult navigation

These conditions exist continuously.

They are fundamental properties of the region.

---

# Magnetic Navigation

Standard navigation methods are unreliable.

Navigation primarily depends on magnetic guidance.

Without a functioning navigation method, determining the correct route becomes extremely difficult.

The exact navigation mechanics are defined in future navigation systems.

---

# Climate Instability

Weather patterns are highly unpredictable.

Multiple climate zones may exist within close proximity.

Possible conditions include:

- Heavy rain
- Extreme heat
- Snowstorms
- Dense fog
- Calm seas
- Violent storms

Environmental changes may occur rapidly.

The AI Game Master should determine weather using the Weather System.

---

# Ocean Conditions

The sea itself presents constant challenges.

Possible hazards include:

- Strong currents
- Whirlpool formation
- Massive waves
- Sudden fog
- Electrical storms
- Reduced visibility

Environmental hazards may exist independently of combat.

---

# Travel Difficulty

Travel through the Grand Line requires significantly greater preparation than travel within the Four Blues.

Factors affecting successful travel include:

- Ship condition
- Crew capability
- Supplies
- Navigation
- Weather
- Sea conditions

Poor preparation greatly increases travel risk.

---

# Island Diversity

Every island within the Grand Line is unique.

Possible differences include:

- Climate
- Culture
- Economy
- Wildlife
- Government
- Technology
- Geography

No standard island template exists.

Each island should be simulated independently.

---

# Isolation

Many islands have limited interaction with neighboring islands.

Trade, culture, and politics may develop independently.

Isolation creates significant regional diversity.

---

# Marine Presence

Marine activity varies throughout the Grand Line.

Some regions are heavily patrolled.

Others receive little governmental attention.

Marine deployment depends on:

- Strategic value
- Crime level
- Political importance
- Trade significance

---

# Pirate Activity

Pirate activity is expected throughout the Grand Line.

The level of activity varies according to:

- Trade routes
- Marine influence
- Local governments
- Available resources
- Territory disputes

Pirate organizations evolve continuously.

---

# Exploration

Exploration is a major component of gameplay.

Players are encouraged to:

- Discover new locations
- Gather information
- Establish relationships
- Trade
- Investigate rumors

Exploration should always involve uncertainty.

Unknown locations should never be fully described before discovery.

---

# Risk and Reward

The Grand Line offers greater opportunities than the Four Blues.

Possible rewards include:

- Rare resources
- Valuable information
- Powerful allies
- Wealth
- Influence

Greater rewards are balanced by significantly greater risks.

---

# World Simulation

The Grand Line continues to evolve regardless of player involvement.

Possible ongoing changes include:

- Political conflict
- Pirate expansion
- Economic shifts
- Island development
- Natural disasters
- Trade route changes

Simulation never pauses.

---

# AI Game Master Responsibilities

The AI must:

- Maintain environmental unpredictability.
- Preserve geographical consistency.
- Simulate regional development.
- Apply realistic travel challenges.
- Respect all established world rules.

The AI must never:

- Make travel completely safe.
- Ignore environmental hazards.
- Simplify navigation without reason.
- Treat every island as identical.

---

# Integration

Parent Documents:

- WORLD.md
- TIMELINE.md
- SEAS.md

Related Documents:

- RED_LINE.md
- CALM_BELT.md
- WEATHER.md
- ISLAND_RULES.md
- WORLD_EVENTS.md

Integrated Systems:

- DICE.md
- COMBAT.md
- MEDICAL.md
- REPUTATION.md
- SAVE_FORMAT.md

---

# Design Principles

The Grand Line exists to reward preparation.

Knowledge is valuable.

Navigation is meaningful.

Exploration is uncertain.

Survival is never guaranteed.

---

# Source of Truth

`GRAND_LINE.md`

is the authoritative specification for all simulation rules concerning the Grand Line.

All future systems involving Grand Line travel, exploration, navigation, and environmental behavior must follow the rules defined in this document.

# ==================================================
# DAWN ISLAND
# ==================================================

Sea: East Blue
Classification: Canon Island
World Type: One Piece Parallel World

---

# OVERVIEW

Dawn Island is one of the largest inhabited islands in East Blue and serves as a major political, agricultural, and military center within the region. Unlike many islands that rely on a single settlement, Dawn Island supports multiple communities connected through established roads, rivers, and maritime trade.

The island is divided into three major regions:

- Goa Kingdom
- Mt. Colubo Region
- Gray Terminal

Each region possesses its own culture, economy, and security concerns, creating opportunities for both cooperation and conflict.

Although regarded as one of the safest islands in East Blue, the contrast between prosperity and poverty has shaped Dawn Island into a land where corruption, ambition, and justice constantly collide.

---

# GEOGRAPHY

Island Size:
Large

Approximate Diameter:
165 km

Travel Time by Foot:
4–5 Days

Highest Elevation:
Mt. Colubo

Terrain Distribution

35% Forest

25% Mountains

20% Plains

10% Rivers

10% Settlements

Coastline

Eastern Coast
White sand beaches and fishing villages.

Northern Coast
Steep cliffs overlooking deep water.

Western Coast
Rocky shoreline with several hidden coves.

Southern Coast
Natural harbors supporting commercial shipping.

---

# CLIMATE

Climate Type

Temperate Oceanic

Spring

Warm winds.

Frequent rainfall.

Excellent farming conditions.

Summer

Hot days.

Strong sunlight.

Occasional tropical storms.

Autumn

Cool temperatures.

Stable seas.

Harvest season.

Winter

Mild compared to northern seas.

Mountain peaks occasionally receive light snowfall.

---

# NATURAL RESOURCES

Primary Resources

Hardwood

Iron Ore

Granite

Fresh Water

Fish

Game Animals

Clay

Medicinal Herbs

Rare Resources

Ancient Stone Tablets

Crystal Veins

Shipbuilding Timber

---

# MAJOR REGIONS

## Goa Kingdom

Political and economic center of Dawn Island.

Contains:

Royal Castle

Central Market

Merchant District

Noble Quarter

Marine Administration Office

Shipwright District

Population

Approximately 42,000

Security Level

Very High

---

## Mt. Colubo

Large mountain region covered by forests.

Wildlife is abundant.

Bandits occasionally establish temporary camps.

Old caves and abandoned mines remain unexplored.

Population

Sparse.

Mostly hunters and woodcutters.

---

## Gray Terminal

Located outside the kingdom walls.

Built from generations of discarded materials, abandoned cargo, broken ships, and salvaged construction.

Despite difficult living conditions, it has developed into a self-governing settlement where traders, scavengers, craftsmen, and laborers survive through informal commerce.

Legal businesses and black-market activity coexist, making the area a constant concern for both the kingdom and the Marines.

Population

Approximately 9,000

Security Level

Low

Marine Presence

Limited patrols.

---

# RIVERS

River Aster

Largest river.

Supports inland trade.

Silver Creek

Mountain water source.

Crystal clear.

Southflow River

Feeds surrounding farmland.

---

# SETTLEMENTS

Dawn Island contains multiple settlements that vary greatly in wealth, security, and culture. Together they form one of East Blue's largest regional economies.

---

## Goa Capital

Type:
Royal Capital

Population:
Approximately 42,000

Description:

The capital is the political heart of Dawn Island. Massive stone walls surround the city, protecting government buildings, noble residences, markets, and military facilities.

Wide streets, canals, and organized districts make it one of the most developed cities in East Blue.

Major Facilities

- Royal Castle
- Central Market
- Marine Administration Office
- Merchant Guild Hall
- Grand Shipyard
- Hospital
- Public Library
- Court of Justice
- Banking House

Primary Occupations

- Government Officials
- Merchants
- Craftsmen
- Shipwrights
- Scholars
- Marines

---

## East Village

Type:
Fishing Village

Population:
Approximately 2,700

Description

A peaceful coastal village known for fishing and small-scale farming.

Residents maintain close relationships with neighboring villages and regularly trade seafood with Goa Capital.

Major Industries

- Fishing
- Boat Repair
- Salt Production

Exports

- Fresh Fish
- Dried Fish
- Sea Salt

---

## Mountain Village

Type:
Mining Settlement

Population:
1,900

Description

Located near Mt. Colubo.

Workers extract iron ore, granite and rare minerals from nearby mountains.

The village frequently hires guards due to attacks from mountain wildlife and bandits.

Industries

- Mining
- Stone Cutting
- Blacksmithing

---

## South Forest Village

Type:
Forestry Community

Population:
3,100

Description

Built among dense forests.

The village specializes in lumber, herbal medicine and hunting.

Many experienced guides originate from this settlement.

Exports

- Hardwood
- Medicine
- Animal Leather
- Herbs

---

## Gray Terminal

Population

Approximately 9,000

Description

Constructed from abandoned cargo, broken ships and salvaged materials.

Despite being considered poor by outsiders, Gray Terminal possesses its own internal economy and leadership.

Residents survive through recycling, repair work, labor, scavenging and informal trade.

Although criminal organizations occasionally operate here, the majority of citizens are ordinary workers attempting to earn an honest living.

Common Businesses

- Scrap Dealers
- Repair Workshops
- Cheap Inns
- Street Markets
- Labor Agencies

---

Dawn Island possesses four operational harbors.

---

## Hidden Cove

Official Status

Unknown

Description

A naturally concealed harbor hidden behind sea cliffs.

Frequently used by smugglers, pirates and illegal traders.

Marine patrols rarely discover unauthorized vessels here.

---

Road Quality

Connects every major settlement.

Primary mining route.

# GOVERNMENT

## Political System

Goa Kingdom is a hereditary constitutional monarchy recognized by the World Government.

While the royal family acts as the symbolic head of state, most administrative affairs are handled by appointed ministers and regional governors.

The kingdom values stability, trade, and cooperation with Marine authorities.

---

## Royal Family

The current royal family has ruled Dawn Island for over two centuries.

Unlike many kingdoms, succession is overseen by the Royal Council to reduce internal conflict.

Royal responsibilities include:

- Foreign diplomacy
- Military authorization
- Appointment of ministers
- Emergency declarations
- Approval of national infrastructure projects

---

## Royal Council

The Royal Council advises the monarch and oversees the kingdom's administration.

Council Departments

- Treasury
- Agriculture
- Commerce
- Infrastructure
- Justice
- Public Health
- Defense
- Harbor Administration

Each department is led by a minister appointed according to merit and experience.

---

## Provincial Administration

Outside the capital, settlements are governed by local administrators.

Responsibilities include:

- Tax collection
- Civil records
- Local policing
- Infrastructure maintenance
- Emergency coordination

Large villages maintain elected advisory councils.

---

# LAW ENFORCEMENT

## Kingdom Guard

The Kingdom Guard serves as the primary civilian security force.

Responsibilities

- Protect government buildings
- Guard city gates
- Patrol marketplaces
- Escort officials
- Maintain public order

Unlike Marines, Kingdom Guards possess no authority outside the island.

---

## Investigation Bureau

A specialized investigative office responsible for major criminal cases.

Jurisdiction

- Murder
- Organized crime
- Corruption
- Large-scale fraud
- Missing persons

The bureau frequently cooperates with Marine investigators.

---

# MARINE PRESENCE

## Overview

Dawn Island hosts one of East Blue's most important Marine installations.

The base supports patrol operations across nearby shipping routes and coordinates emergency responses.

---

## Marine Base

Classification

Regional Branch Base

Personnel

Approximately 450 Marines

Facilities

- Headquarters
- Barracks
- Training Yard
- Prison
- Medical Wing
- Supply Warehouse
- Dry Dock
- Cannon Battery

---

## Standard Patrol Fleet

Harbor Patrol Boats

6

Medium Warships

3

Large Battleship

1

Transport Ships

2

Supply Ships

2

---

## Marine Responsibilities

- Suppress piracy
- Escort merchant fleets
- Protect civilians
- Investigate organized crime
- Respond to natural disasters
- Secure government property

---

## Cooperation

Marines maintain close cooperation with:

- Kingdom Guard
- Harbor Authority
- Merchant Guild
- Medical Association

Joint operations occur regularly during emergencies.

---

# JUSTICE SYSTEM

## Court Structure

Local Court

Handles ordinary criminal and civil cases.

High Court

Reviews major criminal offenses.

Royal Court

Handles constitutional matters and cases affecting national security.

---

## Punishments

Common penalties include:

- Monetary fines
- Community service
- Imprisonment
- Forced labor for severe crimes
- Exile in exceptional circumstances

Capital punishment is extremely rare and reserved for the gravest offenses.

---

# ECONOMY

## Economic Profile

Dawn Island possesses one of the strongest regional economies in East Blue.

Its prosperity is built upon agriculture, shipbuilding, mining, forestry, and maritime trade.

Economic Stability

High

Currency

Belly

Inflation

Low

Employment

High

---

Agriculture

Produces:

Shipbuilding

Produces:

- Fishing Boats
- Merchant Ships
- Patrol Vessels

---

## Merchant Guild

The Merchant Guild regulates trade licenses, shipping contracts, warehouse management, and commercial disputes.

Membership is voluntary but highly respected.

Guild members receive legal protection and trade benefits throughout East Blue.

---

## Taxation

Primary taxes include:

- Harbor Tax
- Trade Tax
- Property Tax
- Import Duty
- Export Duty

Agricultural villages receive seasonal tax reductions after poor harvests.

---

## Banking

Private banking houses provide:

- Currency exchange
- Secure deposits
- Merchant loans
- Letters of credit
- Trade financing

Large transactions rarely use physical cash.

---

# TRADE

## Regional Trade Network

Dawn Island functions as one of East Blue's largest commercial hubs. Merchant vessels depart daily for neighboring islands carrying agricultural products, timber, ore, and manufactured goods.

Major trade is concentrated around the Royal Harbor where customs officials inspect cargo before departure.

Primary Trading Partners

- Shells Town
- Orange Town
- Syrup Village
- Baratie
- Loguetown

Smaller merchant ships also visit remote villages along the coastline.

---

Products

Ships Produced

# CRIME

Overall Crime Level

Low

Urban Crime

Moderate

Rural Crime

Low

Organized Crime

Limited

Common Crimes

- Pickpocketing
- Fraud
- Smuggling
- Illegal Gambling
- Counterfeit Goods
- Warehouse Theft

Violent crime remains uncommon due to active Marine patrols.

---

# BLACK MARKET

Illegal trade exists primarily around Gray Terminal.

Common Contraband

- Stolen Cargo
- Forged Documents
- Illegal Weapons
- Untaxed Alcohol
- Smuggled Medicine

Black-market merchants avoid direct confrontation with Marines.

Most operate through intermediaries.

---

# PIRATE ACTIVITY

Pirate Threat Level

Moderate

Most pirate crews avoid attacking Goa Kingdom directly.

Instead they target

- Merchant Ships
- Fishing Boats
- Coastal Warehouses
- Remote Villages

Typical Crew Size

8–35 Pirates

Average Bounty

5,000,000–18,000,000 Belly

Most crews possess no Haki users.

Devil Fruit users are uncommon.

---

## Pirate Tactics

Common tactics include

- Night Raids
- Coastal Ambushes
- Merchant Hijacking
- Hostage Taking
- Smuggling Cooperation

Well-organized pirate fleets rarely remain near Dawn Island for extended periods because Marine response is rapid.

---

# SECURITY LEVEL

Gray Terminal

★★☆☆☆

★☆☆☆☆

---

# EMERGENCY RESPONSE

Natural Disaster

Kingdom Guard secures settlements.

Marines coordinate evacuation.

Medical Association establishes temporary clinics.

Pirate Attack

Marine Headquarters mobilizes immediately.

Merchant Guild suspends harbor traffic.

Civilian shelters open beneath government buildings.

Disease Outbreak

Harbor quarantine begins.

Medical teams inspect incoming ships.

Trade restrictions may be temporarily enforced.

---

# CULTURE

## General Culture

The people of Dawn Island value hard work, honor, education, and community cooperation.

Unlike many islands dominated by commerce alone, Dawn Island maintains a balance between agriculture, craftsmanship, military service, and scholarship.

Respect for family and local traditions is deeply rooted throughout every settlement.

Children commonly learn practical skills from an early age, including fishing, farming, navigation, carpentry, or trade.

---

## Hospitality

Visitors are generally welcomed warmly.

Travelers who respect local customs often receive assistance from villagers, while criminals quickly attract the attention of both civilians and the Kingdom Guard.

---

## Social Classes

Society naturally divides into several economic groups.

Royal Family

Responsible for national leadership.

---

Nobility

Own large estates and oversee regional development.

Many nobles support charities, although some pursue political influence through wealth.

---

Merchants

One of the most influential social groups.

Successful merchants often finance new businesses, shipyards, and infrastructure.

---

Craftsmen

Highly respected.

Shipwrights, blacksmiths, doctors and carpenters are considered essential professions.

---

Farmers

Provide food security for the island.

Many villages are organized around seasonal harvests.

---

Laborers

Dock workers, miners, hunters and fishermen form the backbone of Dawn Island's economy.

---

# EDUCATION

Education is publicly available throughout the kingdom.

Primary subjects include

- Reading
- Writing
- Mathematics
- Geography
- Maritime Safety
- World Government Law
- Local History

Advanced education is available through private tutors and scholarly institutions within Goa Capital.

---

# RELIGION

There is no official state religion.

Most residents instead maintain local spiritual traditions.

Common beliefs include

- Respect for the sea
- Respect for ancestors
- Seasonal festivals
- Gratitude ceremonies for harvests

Ancient shrines remain scattered throughout forests and mountain regions.

---

# RUMORS

Game Masters may introduce these naturally during conversations.

2. A forgotten tunnel beneath Gray Terminal supposedly leads somewhere beneath the capital.

3. Several merchant ships recently disappeared without distress signals.

4. Someone is secretly purchasing enormous quantities of medical supplies.

5. An abandoned lighthouse has begun glowing again despite being unused for decades.

6. Hunters claim they discovered ruins deeper inside the southern forest.

7. Smugglers have established a new hidden warehouse somewhere along the western cliffs.

8. An ancient stone tablet was recently uncovered during mining operations.

9. Pirates are searching for something rather than treasure.

10. A mysterious traveler has been asking questions about forgotten noble families.

---

---

# ADVENTURE HOOKS

Escort a merchant convoy through dangerous forest roads.

Investigate missing miners inside Mt. Colubo.

Recover stolen medical supplies before disease spreads.

Identify the source of counterfeit Belly coins.

Protect a fishing village from repeated pirate raids.

Search for ancient ruins beneath the southern forest.

Investigate corruption among harbor officials.

Locate a missing Marine reconnaissance patrol.

Discover who finances Gray Terminal's growing black market.

Recover cargo stolen from the Merchant Guild.

---

# HIDDEN LOCATIONS

## Forgotten Watchtower

Deep inside the mountains.

Contains maps dating back more than one hundred years.

---

## Underground Smuggler Tunnel

Connects Gray Terminal with abandoned coastal caves.

Mostly unknown outside criminal circles.

---

## Ancient Shrine

Hidden beneath dense forest.

Covered by enormous tree roots.

Contains inscriptions written in an unknown language.

---

## Crystal Cavern

Accessible only during low tide.

Rare crystals grow naturally within the cave.

Extremely valuable.

---

# SECRETS

Several influential merchants secretly cooperate with smugglers to avoid import taxes.

An abandoned mine beneath Mt. Colubo contains evidence of an unknown civilization predating the current kingdom.

Not every Marine stationed on Dawn Island is loyal to justice.

One member of the Royal Council has secretly financed criminal organizations for years.

The kingdom archives deliberately omit several historical events involving Gray Terminal.

---

# GM NOTES

Recommended Campaign Length

5–15 Sessions

Recommended Player Level

Beginning Characters

Core Themes

- Exploration
- Justice
- Corruption
- Social Inequality
- Maritime Adventure
- Political Intrigue

Dawn Island should introduce players to the everyday life of the One Piece world before exposing them to increasingly dangerous seas.

Every settlement should feel alive.

NPCs should have routines, ambitions, relationships, memories, and personal goals independent of the players.

Player decisions should permanently influence the island.

Merchant prices, Marine patrols, crime rates, public opinion, and political stability may all change as consequences of player actions.

# ==================================================
# EB-002_SHELLS_TOWN
# ==================================================

Sea: East Blue
Classification: Canon Island
World Type: One Piece Parallel World

---

# OVERVIEW

Shells Town is a fortified port city located along one of East Blue's busiest maritime routes.

Unlike Dawn Island, whose economy is supported by agriculture and natural resources, Shells Town exists primarily because of its military importance.

The city developed around a Marine Base that gradually attracted merchants, craftsmen, shipbuilders and travelers seeking protection from piracy.

Today it serves as one of the strongest Marine-controlled ports in East Blue.

Its streets are orderly, commerce is active, and law enforcement is strict.

However, beneath its disciplined appearance, political tension, organized crime and corruption continue to threaten the city's stability.

---

# GEOGRAPHY

Island Classification

Medium Island

Diameter

Approximately 72 km

Terrain

40% Hills

25% Forest

20% Urban Area

10% Farmland

5% Rocky Coast

Highest Point

Fort Sentinel Hill

Major Rivers

Clearwater River

Blue Stream

Natural Harbor

One large deep-water harbor.

Suitable for Marine Battleships.

---

# CLIMATE

Type

Warm Maritime

Spring

Pleasant temperatures.

Light rain.

Summer

Hot.

Occasional tropical storms.

Autumn

Cool sea breeze.

Stable weather.

Winter

Mild.

Rarely below 15°C.

Navigation remains possible throughout the year.

---

# HISTORY

Originally established as a small fishing settlement.

After repeated pirate attacks, the World Government constructed a Marine fortress overlooking the harbor.

Merchants quickly settled nearby due to increased security.

Within several decades Shells Town became one of East Blue's largest military ports.

Today nearly every aspect of the city's economy depends on maritime trade and Marine logistics.

---

# DISTRICTS

## Marine District

The oldest district.

Contains

- Marine Headquarters
- Training Grounds
- Barracks
- Prison
- Armory
- Cannon Batteries

Civilian access is restricted.

---

Center of commercial activity.

Contains

- Warehouses

- Customs Office

Merchant ships arrive throughout the day.

---

## Old Market

Historic commercial district.

Filled with

- Restaurants
- Inns
- Tailors
- Blacksmiths
- General Stores

Busy from sunrise until evening.

---

## Residential Quarter

Home to most civilians.

Contains schools, clinics, parks and temples.

Crime remains low due to frequent patrols.

---

## Hill District

Located near Fort Sentinel.

Home to wealthy merchants, senior officers and influential families.

Large stone houses overlook the harbor.

---

# GOVERNMENT

## Administrative Structure

Shells Town is governed jointly by the Town Council and the Marine Regional Headquarters.

While civilian matters remain under local jurisdiction, military affairs are controlled entirely by the Marines.

The cooperation between both institutions has transformed Shells Town into one of East Blue's safest ports.

---

# FILE : 01_WORLD\ISLANDS\EAST_BLUE\EB-003_EMBER_REEF.md
# =====================================================

# ==================================================
# EMBER REEF
# ==================================================

Sea: East Blue
Classification: Original Island
World Type: One Piece Parallel World

---

# OVERVIEW

Ember Reef is a sprawling coral reef archipelago located along one of East Blue's secondary maritime routes. Unlike conventional islands, Ember Reef is composed of dozens of rocky islets, coral shelves, tidal lagoons, underwater caverns, and narrow natural channels that weave between sharp reefs.

Most navigators avoid the area unless absolutely necessary. Hidden reefs, unpredictable currents, and shallow waters make large vessels extremely vulnerable.

Despite these dangers, Ember Reef has developed into a modest but thriving maritime community. Local residents have mastered reef navigation over generations and serve as pilots, fishermen, salvagers, pearl divers, lighthouse keepers, and ship repair specialists.

Because of its geography, Ember Reef has become a refuge for travelers during storms, while also attracting smugglers, treasure hunters, pirates, and adventurers seeking forgotten shipwrecks beneath the sea.

Although officially recognized by the World Government, Marine influence remains limited due to the complexity of the surrounding waters.

---

# HISTORY

## Early Settlement

The first permanent inhabitants arrived more than two hundred years ago after several merchant vessels were destroyed by the surrounding reefs.

Rather than abandoning the dangerous waters, survivors established small fishing villages upon the largest coral islands where fresh water could be collected naturally through underground limestone reservoirs.

Over time these isolated communities learned to survive using the sea itself.

Fishing.

Coral harvesting.

Salt production.

Shell collecting.

Boat construction.

Navigation.

became the foundations of Ember Reef society.

---

## Age of Sail

As maritime trade expanded throughout East Blue, experienced pilots from Ember Reef became highly respected.

Large merchant fleets frequently hired local navigators capable of safely guiding ships through dangerous reef passages.

This profession transformed Ember Reef from an isolated fishing settlement into an important waypoint for commercial shipping.

Several lighthouse towers were constructed during this era.

Many still operate today.

---

## The Wreck Years

Approximately sixty years ago a succession of unusually violent storms devastated the region.

Hundreds of vessels struck hidden reefs.

The sea floor surrounding Ember Reef became littered with shipwrecks.

Many wrecks remain unexplored.

These sunken vessels continue attracting treasure hunters from across East Blue.

Local law strictly regulates salvage rights to prevent violent disputes.

---

## Modern Era

Today Ember Reef maintains peaceful relations with neighboring islands.

Its economy relies primarily upon:

- Fishing
- Navigation Services
- Salvage Operations
- Pearl Diving
- Coral Craftsmanship
- Boat Repair

The settlement has intentionally avoided rapid expansion to preserve its fragile ecosystem.

---

# GEOGRAPHY

Island Type

Coral Reef Archipelago

Approximate Diameter

78 km

Navigable Waters

Only 35% of surrounding waters are considered safe for medium-sized vessels without local guidance.

---

## Terrain Distribution

Coral Reefs
42%

Shallow Lagoons
18%

Rocky Islets
16%

White Sand Beaches
8%

Mangrove Forests
7%

Sea Caves
5%

Settlements
4%

---

## Coastline

Northern Reefs

Dense coral fields.

Very shallow.

Dangerous during low tide.

---

Eastern Lagoon

Calm turquoise waters.

Used for fishing and training young sailors.

---

Southern Cliffs

Tall limestone cliffs overlooking deep ocean currents.

Numerous seabird nesting grounds.

---

Western Passage

Primary shipping lane.

Marked by stone beacons and lighthouse towers.

---

# NATURAL LANDMARKS

## Ember Lighthouse

The oldest structure within the archipelago.

Visible from over thirty kilometers during clear weather.

Still manually operated.

---

## Crimson Coral Garden

A massive coral forest colored deep red by unusual marine algae.

Protected by local law.

Harvesting coral is prohibited.

---

## Whisper Caverns

A network of underwater limestone caves.

Strong currents produce haunting echoes.

Divers frequently report becoming disoriented.

---

## Broken Mast Reef

The remains of numerous ancient shipwrecks.

Fragments of masts still protrude above the sea during low tide.

Considered sacred by local fishermen.

---

## Tide Mirror Lagoon

Perfectly still water during calm mornings.

Widely used for celestial navigation training.

---

# CLIMATE

Climate Classification

Tropical Maritime

Average Temperature

24°C–33°C

Humidity

High

Rainfall

Moderate throughout the year.

Storm Season

Late Summer

---

## Spring

Gentle winds.

Excellent visibility.

Peak fishing season.

---

## Summer

Warm temperatures.

Occasional tropical storms.

Powerful tidal currents.

---

## Autumn

Stable weather.

Ideal sailing conditions.

Merchant traffic increases significantly.

---

## Winter

Cool sea breeze.

Frequent morning fog.

Calm waters inside lagoons.

Open sea remains unpredictable.

---

# OCEAN CONDITIONS

Average Wave Height

0.5–2 meters

Storm Waves

Up to 7 meters

Average Visibility

Excellent

Night Navigation

Moderate difficulty.

Requires lighthouse guidance.

---

# TIDAL SYSTEM

Ember Reef experiences unusually strong tidal movement.

Every twelve hours:

- Hidden reefs emerge.
- Sea caves become accessible.
- Certain navigation routes disappear.
- Shipwrecks may briefly surface.

Experienced captains plan voyages according to local tide charts.

Inexperienced navigators often become stranded.

# END OF PART 1

---

# NATURAL RESOURCES

## Marine Resources

Ember Reef possesses one of the richest shallow-water ecosystems in East Blue.

Commercial Fishing

- Tuna
- Mackerel
- Snapper
- Grouper
- Flying Fish
- Sardines
- Reef Shrimp
- Lobster
- Octopus
- Squid

Shellfish

- Giant Clams
- Oysters
- Mussels
- Scallops
- Sea Snails

Sea Plants

- Seaweed
- Kelp
- Edible Algae
- Medicinal Sea Moss

---

## Coral Resources

Only licensed harvesters may collect dead coral.

Living coral is protected.

Commercial Products

- Decorative Coral
- Coral Limestone
- Coral Powder
- Jewelry Material

Illegal harvesting carries severe penalties.

---

## Mineral Resources

Although the islands themselves contain little metal ore, limestone formations provide valuable construction material.

Resources

- Limestone
- White Sand
- Coral Stone
- Marble Fragments
- Sea Salt

---

## Rare Resources

Black Pearl Oyster

Occurs naturally within deeper lagoons.

Extremely valuable.

---

Blue Coral

A rare living coral species believed to purify seawater.

Protected.

---

Sea Crystal

Transparent mineral occasionally discovered inside underwater caves.

Used by craftsmen for expensive ornaments.

---

Protected ecological reserve.

Marine scientists occasionally visit.

Fishing prohibited.

---

# SETTLEMENTS

## Ember Harbor

Type

Harbor Town

Population

3,600

Description

The largest community in Ember Reef.

Built upon interconnected wooden platforms, stone foundations and elevated walkways.

Most buildings overlook the sea.

Residents travel primarily by small boats.

Major Facilities

- Harbor Office
- Marketplace
- Boat Repair Yard
- Fish Auction
- Medical Clinic
- Navigation School
- Warehouse District
- Marine Outpost
- Public Inn

---

## Coral Village

Type

Fishing Village

Population

1,400

Description

A quiet settlement famous for skilled pearl divers.

Families have lived here for generations.

Buildings are constructed using coral stone and hardwood.

Major Facilities

- Pearl Market
- Smokehouse
- Community Dock
- Diving Guild

---

## Lighthouse Point

Type

Service Settlement

Population

380

Description

Supports lighthouse operations and weather observation.

Residents monitor storms and warn nearby vessels.

Facilities

- Lighthouse
- Weather Station
- Emergency Shelter
- Supply Depot

---

# ROAD NETWORK

Roads are limited.

Transportation occurs primarily by water.

Wooden bridges connect nearby islets.

Long-distance travel requires boats.

---

## Main Routes

Harbor Walk

Connects the commercial district with residential areas.

---

Coral Bridge

Links Ember Harbor to Coral Village.

Accessible during all tides.

---

Mangrove Trail

Wooden pathway through coastal wetlands.

Frequently damaged by storms.

---

Lighthouse Route

Stone road leading uphill toward Ember Lighthouse.

Steep but well maintained.

---

# DEMOGRAPHIC CHARACTERISTICS

# END OF PART 2
---

# GOVERNMENT

## Administrative Structure

Ember Reef is governed by the **Reef Council**, a civilian administration composed of representatives elected from each major settlement.

Rather than maintaining a centralized monarchy or noble hierarchy, the council focuses on practical governance, maritime safety, environmental protection, and commercial regulation.

The council meets every month within Ember Harbor.

Primary Responsibilities

- Harbor administration
- Fishing regulations
- Environmental protection
- Maritime taxation
- Public infrastructure
- Emergency response
- Navigation safety
- Trade licensing

---

## Reef Council

Number of Representatives

7

Departments

- Harbor Affairs
- Fisheries
- Trade
- Public Works
- Civil Security
- Environmental Conservation
- Emergency Management

Council members serve four-year terms.

---

## Harbor Authority

The Harbor Authority manages all incoming and outgoing maritime traffic.

Responsibilities

- Dock assignments
- Cargo inspections
- Ship registration
- Harbor maintenance
- Navigation permits
- Lighthouse coordination

---

# LAW ENFORCEMENT

## Reef Guard

Ember Reef maintains its own civilian security force known as the Reef Guard.

Personnel

Approximately 140

Primary Duties

- Harbor patrol
- Crime prevention
- Rescue operations
- Crowd control
- Wildlife protection
- Emergency evacuation

Unlike Marines, the Reef Guard possesses no authority outside Ember Reef.

---

## Harbor Patrol

The Harbor Patrol specializes in maritime enforcement.

Fleet

- 8 Patrol Boats
- 3 Rescue Boats
- 2 Medical Boats

Responsibilities

- Search and rescue
- Anti-smuggling patrols
- Navigation assistance
- Harbor inspections

---

# MARINE PRESENCE

## Marine Outpost

Classification

Forward Observation Station

Personnel

Approximately 55 Marines

Purpose

Rather than serving as a military base, the Marine presence focuses on maintaining safe trade routes through the reef.

Facilities

- Barracks
- Communications Tower
- Small Prison
- Supply Warehouse
- Medical Room
- Observation Deck

---

## Patrol Fleet

2 Patrol Ships

3 Fast Boats

1 Supply Vessel

---

## Marine Responsibilities

- Suppress piracy
- Investigate maritime crimes
- Escort merchant convoys
- Assist during storms
- Coordinate rescue missions

Relations with civilians are generally positive.

---

# JUSTICE SYSTEM

Minor offenses are handled locally.

Serious crimes are transferred to Marine jurisdiction.

Common Punishments

- Monetary fines
- Community service
- Temporary labor
- Imprisonment
- Confiscation of illegal property

Environmental crimes receive especially severe penalties.

Illegal coral harvesting is considered a major offense.

---

# ECONOMY

Economic Stability

High

Primary Currency

Belly

Economic Focus

Maritime industries.

The economy depends heavily upon the sea rather than agriculture.

Major Industries

- Commercial Fishing
- Pearl Diving
- Boat Construction
- Navigation Services
- Salvage Operations
- Coral Craftsmanship
- Salt Production

---

## Fishing Industry

Fishing remains Ember Reef's largest employer.

Commercial Products

- Fresh Fish
- Dried Fish
- Smoked Fish
- Salted Seafood

Exports travel throughout East Blue.

---

## Pearl Industry

Licensed divers harvest pearls from protected oyster beds.

Black Pearls

Rare

Highly valuable.

Sold only through government auctions.

---

## Ship Repair

Large dry docks cannot be constructed because of shallow waters.

Instead, skilled craftsmen specialize in repairing

- Fishing Boats
- Merchant Ships
- Patrol Boats
- Sailing Vessels

Emergency repairs are available year-round.

---

## Navigation Services

Perhaps Ember Reef's most respected profession.

Licensed pilots guide merchant fleets through dangerous reef passages.

Pilot fees provide significant income for local communities.

---

## Coral Crafts

Dead coral collected legally is transformed into

- Jewelry
- Decorative Art
- Furniture
- Building Materials

Living coral cannot be harvested.

---

# TRADE

Primary Exports

- Seafood
- Pearls
- Coral Crafts

- Boat Parts
- Navigation Charts

Primary Imports

- Grain
- Timber
- Steel
- Medicine
- Cloth

Major Trading Partners

- Orange Town
- Shells Town
- Loguetown
- Baratie
- Dawn Island

Merchant vessels typically arrive every three to five days.

# CRIME

Overall Crime Level

Low

Ember Reef is considered one of the safer maritime settlements in East Blue. Most crimes involve illegal trade rather than violent offenses.

Crime Distribution

Commercial District
★★★☆☆

Fishing Villages
★☆☆☆☆

Lighthouse Point
★☆☆☆☆

Outer Reefs
★★★☆☆

Uninhabited Islets
★★★★☆

---

## Common Crimes

- Smuggling
- Illegal Salvaging
- Tax Evasion
- Navigation Fraud
- Theft of Fishing Equipment
- Coral Poaching
- Forged Trade Licenses

Violent crime is uncommon due to the close-knit communities.

---

## Smuggling

The intricate reef network provides countless hidden routes.

Common Smuggled Goods

- Untaxed Alcohol
- Illegal Weapons
- Counterfeit Belly
- Rare Medicines
- Exotic Animals

Smugglers generally avoid conflict and rely on secrecy.

---

## Illegal Salvage

Many ancient shipwrecks remain protected by law.

Treasure hunters occasionally violate salvage regulations.

Recovered artifacts are confiscated if discovered.

---

# BLACK MARKET

The Black Market operates discreetly from abandoned warehouses hidden among remote reefs.

Unlike larger criminal organizations found elsewhere in the world, Ember Reef's underground economy consists of numerous independent traders.

Illegal Goods

- Forged Navigation Charts
- Counterfeit Sea Maps
- Smuggled Medicines
- Illegal Coral
- Ship Components
- Stolen Cargo

Risk Level

Moderate

Marine Crackdowns

Occasional

---

# PIRATE ACTIVITY

Pirate Threat Level

★★★☆☆

Most pirate crews avoid attacking Ember Harbor directly.

Instead they use the surrounding reefs as temporary hiding places while repairing damaged ships or avoiding Marine pursuit.

Typical Crew Size

10–40 Pirates

Average Bounty

5,000,000 – 18,000,000 Belly

Most possess no Haki.

Devil Fruit users are uncommon.

---

## Pirate Strategies

Common tactics include

- Ambushing merchant ships
- Hiding among reefs
- Attacking isolated fishing boats
- Stealing navigation charts
- Using abandoned shipwrecks as temporary bases

---

# SECURITY LEVEL

Ember Harbor

★★★★★

Coral Village

★★★★☆

★★☆☆☆

Whisper Caverns

★☆☆☆☆

Open Sea

★★☆☆☆

---

# EMERGENCY RESPONSE

## Storm Response

When severe storms approach:

- Lighthouse warning signals are activated.
- Harbor closes immediately.
- Fishing boats return to port.
- Emergency shelters open.
- Marine patrols suspend normal operations.

---

## Pirate Attack

Harbor bells alert every district.

The Reef Guard secures civilians.

Marine vessels protect shipping lanes.

Merchant ships remain docked until cleared.

---

## Tsunami Warning

Although rare, underwater earthquakes occasionally generate dangerous waves.

Emergency procedures include

- Immediate evacuation to elevated ground.
- Harbor lockdown.
- Medical stations activated.
- Food warehouses opened.

---

# CULTURE

The people of Ember Reef live according to the rhythm of the sea.

Navigation, weather, and tides influence daily life far more than calendars.

Children begin learning sailing before reaching adolescence.

Nearly every household owns at least one small boat.

Hospitality toward travelers is valued, particularly toward sailors caught in storms.

---

## Traditions

Local traditions emphasize respect for the sea.

Common beliefs include

- Never whistle during storms.
- Always thank the sea after a safe voyage.
- Leave offerings before long expeditions.
- Rescue anyone in distress regardless of affiliation.

---

## Clothing

Residents favor lightweight maritime clothing.

Typical attire

- Linen Shirts
- Waterproof Boots
- Wide Hats
- Rope Belts
- Oilskin Coats
- Coral Jewelry

---

# EDUCATION

Education focuses on practical maritime knowledge.

Children study

- Reading
- Mathematics
- Geography
- Navigation
- Weather Observation
- Boat Maintenance
- Marine Ecology

Advanced navigation courses attract students from neighboring islands.

---

# RELIGION

No organized religion exists.

Instead, local customs revolve around honoring nature.

Small shrines dedicated to the sea are found throughout the archipelago.

Many sailors leave shells or flowers before departing on long voyages.

---

# FESTIVALS

## Tide Festival

Celebrated during the calmest tides of the year.

Activities

- Boat Racing
- Seafood Market
- Music
- Dancing
- Lantern Ceremony

---

## Pearl Moon Festival

Held once each year.

Licensed divers display their finest pearls.

Visitors from throughout East Blue attend.

---

## Lighthouse Night

A celebration honoring generations of lighthouse keepers.

Every lighthouse burns continuously until sunrise.

---

# FOOD

Daily Meals

Breakfast

- Bread
- Smoked Fish
- Fruit

Lunch

- Rice
- Seafood Soup
- Seaweed Salad

Dinner

- Grilled Fish
- Shellfish
- Vegetables
- Coconut Desserts

---

# LOCAL SPECIALTIES

Ember Seafood Stew

Prepared using several species of reef fish.

---

Black Pearl Oyster

Luxury dish served only during festivals.

---

Sea Salt Bread

Baked using locally harvested sea salt.

---

Coral Shrimp Skewers

Popular among travelers.

# END OF PART 4
---

# FLORA

Although Ember Reef contains limited landmass, its plant life has adapted exceptionally well to the harsh marine environment.

The vegetation plays a vital role in preventing coastal erosion and supporting marine ecosystems.

---

## Coastal Trees

### Coconut Palm

The most common tree throughout the archipelago.

Uses

- Food
- Drinking Water
- Construction
- Rope
- Fuel

---

### Iron Mangrove

A hardy mangrove species capable of surviving constant saltwater exposure.

Its roots stabilize coastlines and provide breeding grounds for countless marine animals.

Wood is extremely durable.

---

### Salt Pine

A wind-resistant conifer growing upon rocky cliffs.

Frequently used in lighthouse construction.

---

## Medicinal Plants

### Sea Moss

Collected from shallow reefs.

Used for

- Fever Medicine
- Burn Treatment
- Nutritional Supplements

---

### Coral Mint

A fragrant coastal herb.

Produces cooling medicinal oil.

Commonly used against seasickness.

---

### Tide Fern

Grows only during high tide.

Used by physicians for wound treatment.

---

### Blue Kelp

Cultivated in underwater farms.

Applications

- Food
- Medicine
- Fertilizer

---

## Rare Plants

### Moon Coral Flower

Blooms only during nights with a full moon.

Its petals glow faintly.

Highly valued by botanists.

---

### Glass Sea Orchid

Found inside sea caves.

Extremely difficult to cultivate.

Collectors pay enormous prices.

---

# WILDLIFE

## Common Animals

Sea Birds

Large colonies inhabit the cliffs.

---

Hermit Crabs

Found across sandy beaches.

---

Island Foxes

Small scavengers.

Harmless.

---

Fruit Bats

Help pollinate coastal vegetation.

---

Reef Lizards

Excellent climbers.

Often seen around docks.

---

# DANGEROUS WILDLIFE

Reef Sharks

Normally avoid humans.

Become aggressive when food is scarce.

---

Giant Moray Eels

Hide inside coral formations.

Can exceed five meters.

---

Stoneback Sea Turtle

Generally peaceful.

Can accidentally overturn small boats.

---

Sea Serpents

Rare.

Large marine predators occasionally observed offshore.

---

Poison Lionfish

Beautiful but venomous.

Divers exercise extreme caution.

---

# SEA LIFE

Ember Reef contains one of East Blue's richest marine ecosystems.

Species include

- Flying Fish
- Bluefin Tuna
- Swordfish
- Mackerel
- Snapper
- Barracuda
- Lobster
- Octopus
- Squid
- Dolphins
- Sea Turtles
- Seahorses
- Rays

Coral reefs shelter hundreds of smaller species.

---

# NATURAL HAZARDS

The environment itself presents Ember Reef's greatest danger.

Common Hazards

- Hidden Coral Reefs
- Powerful Tidal Currents
- Sudden Storms
- Dense Sea Fog
- Whirlpool Formation
- Slippery Cliffs
- Underwater Sinkholes

---

## Seasonal Storms

Late summer frequently brings violent tropical storms.

Travel is often suspended.

Fishing fleets remain docked.

---

## Rogue Waves

Occasionally generated by underwater terrain.

Can capsize even medium-sized vessels.

---

## Coral Cuts

Many visitors underestimate coral.

Minor injuries frequently become infected if untreated.

---

Unauthorized salvage is prohibited.

Influence

Protects pearl beds and licenses professional divers.

Maintains sustainable harvesting practices.

Influence

★★★★☆

Responsible for maintaining every beacon throughout the archipelago.

Members monitor

- Weather

- Incoming Ships

# LOCAL RUMORS

Game Masters may introduce these naturally during adventures.

1. A merchant ship vanished inside the reef without leaving any wreckage.

2. Strange lights appear beneath Tide Mirror Lagoon every full moon.

3. Divers discovered an ancient staircase descending beneath the sea.

4. Someone has begun stealing official navigation charts.

5. Several pearl divers claim they heard bells ringing beneath the ocean floor.

6. Smugglers are paying enormous sums for experienced local pilots.

7. A forgotten lighthouse somewhere beyond Broken Mast Reef still burns at night.

8. Giant shadows occasionally move beneath fishing boats.

9. Marine investigators recently confiscated an unidentified artifact recovered from a shipwreck.

10. Local fishermen refuse to sail near Whisper Caverns after sunset.

---

Roll 1D20 while traveling around Ember Reef.

| Roll | Encounter |
|------|-----------|
|1|A merchant vessel requests a local guide.|
|2|A fishing net catches a mysterious locked chest.|
|3|Heavy fog suddenly reduces visibility.|
|4|Marine patrol performs inspections.|

|6|A wounded sea turtle washes ashore.|
|7|A pod of dolphins follows the ship.|
|8|A coral cave becomes accessible due to low tide.|
|9|A lighthouse signal warns of an approaching storm.|

|12|Pirate scouts observe from distant reefs.|

|14|A traveling merchant offers rare nautical equipment.|
|15|Someone attempts to sell an old treasure map.|
|16|Flying fish leap across the ship's bow.|
|17|Children race homemade sailboats near the harbor.|
|18|A damaged merchant ship seeks immediate repairs.|

|20|A hidden entrance to an underwater cave is revealed during low tide.|

# ADVENTURE HOOKS

## The Silent Convoy

Several merchant ships scheduled to arrive at Ember Harbor never appear.

No distress signals were received.

The players are hired to investigate the last known shipping route.

Possible Outcomes

- Shipwreck Discovery
- Pirate Ambush
- Smuggling Operation
- Natural Disaster

---

## The Missing Lighthouse Flame

The Ember Lighthouse suddenly stops operating.

Without its beacon, dozens of merchant ships refuse to approach the reef.

Players must determine whether the cause is sabotage, accident, or something hidden beneath the lighthouse.

---

## Coral Thieves

Living coral has begun disappearing despite strict protection laws.

The Reef Council fears permanent ecological damage.

The players investigate illegal harvesting operations hidden among remote reefs.

---

## The Pearl Auction

The annual Black Pearl Auction attracts merchants from across East Blue.

During the event, an extremely valuable pearl disappears.

Every guest becomes a suspect.

---

## The Broken Chart

A famous navigator dies unexpectedly, leaving behind only half of an unfinished sea chart.

Rumors suggest it reveals a forgotten route through Ember Reef.

Several organizations begin searching for the missing half.

---

## Echoes Beneath the Sea

Divers exploring Whisper Caverns report hearing human voices beneath the ocean floor.

Several never return.

The Reef Council requests an expedition.

---

---

# HIDDEN LOCATIONS

## The Forgotten Beacon

An abandoned lighthouse standing upon an isolated reef.

Its beacon occasionally shines despite having no keeper.

---

## Smuggler's Hollow

A concealed sea cave accessible only during low tide.

Contains hidden docks and storage rooms.

---

## Coral Cathedral

A massive underwater coral formation resembling a cathedral.

Schools of colorful fish gather here throughout the year.

Many divers consider it sacred.

---

## The Glass Lagoon

A perfectly transparent lagoon surrounded by limestone cliffs.

The seabed can be seen even at great depth.

Very few outsiders know of its existence.

---

# SECRETS

Only the Game Master should know these details unless discovered naturally.

Secret 1

Several official navigation charts intentionally omit certain safe passages.

This allows licensed pilots to maintain their monopoly.

---

Secret 2

One respected merchant secretly finances local smugglers while publicly supporting Marine operations.

---

Secret 3

A forgotten shipwreck beneath Broken Mast Reef contains records from more than one hundred years ago.

Its historical value exceeds its treasure.

---

Secret 4

Whisper Caverns connect to a much larger underwater cave system extending far beyond Ember Reef.

No complete map exists.

---

Secret 5

The Reef Council quietly maintains emergency food reserves inside hidden limestone caverns for use after catastrophic storms.

---

# ==================================================
# ORANGE TOWN
# ==================================================

Sea: East Blue
Classification: Canon Island
World Type: One Piece Parallel World

---

# OVERVIEW

Orange Town is one of East Blue's oldest commercial port cities and serves as an important regional trading center connecting numerous nearby islands.

Unlike heavily fortified government cities, Orange Town developed through commerce rather than military expansion. Its streets are densely packed with shops, workshops, warehouses, inns, restaurants and merchant offices, making it one of the busiest civilian settlements in the sea.

Because thousands of travelers pass through every month, Orange Town has become a melting pot of cultures, professions and information.

Although generally peaceful, the constant flow of money also attracts smugglers, thieves and organized criminals.

---

# HISTORY

## Early Settlement

The first settlers established Orange Town nearly two centuries ago around a naturally protected harbor.

Fishing and coastal trade quickly transformed the settlement into an important marketplace.

---

## Merchant Expansion

As maritime trade throughout East Blue increased, merchant families invested heavily in warehouses, docks and public infrastructure.

Roads were expanded.

New districts emerged.

Population steadily increased.

---

## Modern Era

Orange Town now serves as one of East Blue's busiest civilian ports.

Merchant vessels arrive almost daily carrying food, timber, ore, textiles and manufactured goods.

Rather than depending upon one major industry, Orange Town prospers through diversified commerce.

---

Type

Commercial City

The city's economic heart.

Street performers, traveling merchants and adventurers are common sights.

# GOVERNMENT

## Political System

Orange Town is administered by an elected Town Council recognized by the World Government.

Unlike kingdoms, Orange Town is governed through civic administration focused on commerce, taxation and public welfare.

---

## Town Council

Departments

- Finance
- Trade
- Harbor Affairs
- Public Safety
- Infrastructure
- Agriculture
- Public Health
- Education

The council meets every two weeks.

Major decisions require majority approval.

---

## Harbor Authority

The Harbor Authority operates independently from the Town Council.

Responsibilities

- Dock Assignment
- Customs Inspection
- Cargo Registration
- Navigation Safety
- Harbor Maintenance

---

# LAW ENFORCEMENT

## City Guard

Personnel

Approximately 320

Responsibilities

- Patrol Markets
- Protect Citizens
- Investigate Theft
- Escort Government Officials
- Maintain Public Order

Equipment

- Flintlock Pistols
- Riot Shields

---

## Harbor Security Division

Responsible for crimes involving ships and cargo.

Personnel

95 Officers

Duties

- Cargo Inspection
- Anti-Smuggling
- Dock Patrol
- Customs Enforcement

---

## Investigation Office

Handles serious criminal cases.

Jurisdiction

- Murder
- Organized Crime
- Fraud
- Corruption
- Missing Persons
- Counterfeiting

Frequently cooperates with Marines.

---

# JUSTICE SYSTEM

Court Structure

Handles civil disputes and ordinary crimes.

---

Specialized court for trade conflicts.

---

Handles major criminal cases.

---

Punishments

- Monetary Fines
- Property Confiscation
- Community Service
- Imprisonment
- Forced Labor for Severe Crimes

Capital punishment is nearly nonexistent.

# TAXATION

Commercial Tax

Applied to all registered businesses.

Harbor Tax

Collected from every docking vessel.

Import Duty

Based upon cargo value.

Export Duty

Reduced for agricultural products.

Warehouse Fee

Charged according to storage duration.

Tax exemptions may be granted following natural disasters.

---

# CRIME

Overall Crime Level

★★★☆☆

Orange Town maintains a relatively safe environment compared to many commercial ports throughout East Blue. However, its prosperity naturally attracts criminal organizations seeking profit.

Most criminal activity centers around financial crimes rather than violence.

---

## Common Crimes

- Pickpocketing
- Fraud
- Cargo Theft
- Smuggling
- Forged Documents
- Counterfeit Belly
- Warehouse Burglary
- Illegal Gambling

---

## Organized Crime

Several independent criminal groups operate within Orange Town.

Rather than controlling territory openly, they specialize in

- Smuggling
- Black Market Trading
- Cargo Theft
- Financial Fraud

These groups constantly compete against one another.

Violent conflict inside the city is uncommon because it attracts Marine attention.

---

## Smuggling

Due to the enormous volume of cargo entering the harbor every day, smugglers frequently attempt to conceal illegal goods among legitimate shipments.

Common Contraband

- Illegal Weapons
- Rare Medicines
- Untaxed Alcohol
- Stolen Artwork
- Counterfeit Navigation Charts

---

## Financial Crime

Orange Town's large banking sector makes it a target for sophisticated fraud.

Recent investigations include

- Forged Merchant Licenses
- Fake Shipping Contracts
- Counterfeit Currency
- Insurance Fraud

---

# BLACK MARKET

Although officially prohibited, a hidden underground economy exists beneath portions of the Harbor District.

Access requires trusted contacts.

Illegal Services

- Forged Identification
- Smuggled Cargo
- Unregistered Ships
- Stolen Navigation Logs
- Illegal Auctions

Most transactions occur late at night.

---

# PIRATE ACTIVITY

Pirate Threat Level

★★★☆☆

Few pirate crews attack Orange Town directly.

Instead they prefer ambushing merchant vessels shortly after departure.

Average Crew Size

10–45 Pirates

Average Bounty

6,000,000–22,000,000 Belly

Most crews possess no Haki users.

Devil Fruit users remain uncommon.

---

## Pirate Strategies

Typical attacks include

- Merchant Ambushes
- Cargo Hijacking
- Hostage Taking
- Coastal Raids
- Warehouse Robbery

Large pirate fleets rarely remain near Orange Town due to rapid Marine response.

---

# SECURITY LEVEL

Central District

★★★★★

Merchant Quarter

★★★★☆

Harbor District

★★★★☆

Residential Areas

★★★★☆

Industrial Zone

★★★☆☆

Outer Farmland

★★★☆☆

Abandoned Warehouses

★★☆☆☆

---

# EMERGENCY RESPONSE

## Fire Response

Orange Town maintains multiple public water towers.

Fire brigades respond within minutes inside the city.

Wooden warehouse districts remain high-risk areas.

---

## Pirate Attack

Harbor gates close immediately.

Marine ships deploy.

Merchant traffic is suspended.

Citizens are evacuated toward reinforced public shelters.

---

## Severe Storm

Lighthouse warning systems activate.

Ships receive emergency docking priority.

Public warehouses distribute food reserves if necessary.

---

## Disease Outbreak

Medical checkpoints are established at every harbor entrance.

Incoming crews undergo inspection.

Temporary quarantine may be declared.

---

# CULTURE

Orange Town is known throughout East Blue as a city where nearly every culture can be encountered.

Merchants, craftsmen, sailors and travelers from numerous islands gather here daily.

The city's identity revolves around commerce, hospitality and opportunity.

Hard work is respected more than noble birth.

Business reputation is considered extremely important.

---

## Daily Life

Typical daily activities include

- Street Markets
- Public Auctions
- Harbor Commerce
- Artisan Workshops
- Outdoor Cafés
- Traveling Performers

The city remains active from sunrise until late evening.

---

## Hospitality

Visitors are generally welcomed warmly.

Honest merchants earn long-term trust quickly.

Known criminals find it difficult to conduct business openly.

---

## Clothing

Typical attire includes

- Linen Shirts
- Merchant Coats
- Leather Boots
- Utility Belts
- Wide-Brimmed Hats

Dock workers typically wear heavier protective clothing.

---

# EDUCATION

Orange Town operates one of East Blue's most respected public education systems.

Primary Subjects

- Reading
- Writing
- Mathematics
- Geography
- Commerce
- Navigation
- Law
- Accounting

Advanced vocational schools train

- Shipwrights
- Doctors
- Merchants
- Accountants
- Navigators

---

# RELIGION

Orange Town has no official religion.

Most residents instead maintain local family traditions.

Small shrines dedicated to safe voyages are scattered throughout the harbor.

Many sailors leave flowers or seashells before long expeditions.

---

# FESTIVALS

## Grand Trade Festival

Held once each year.

Celebrates commerce throughout East Blue.

Activities

- Merchant Exhibitions
- Public Auctions
- Street Food
- Music
- Fireworks

---

## Harbor Festival

Honors sailors and dock workers.

Features

- Boat Racing
- Rope Competitions
- Cargo Lifting Contests
- Ship Decoration Awards

---

## Harvest Fair

Local farmers bring produce into the city.

Markets expand throughout the central plaza.

Fresh foods are sold at reduced prices.

---

# FLORA

Orange Town possesses fertile soil and a mild maritime climate, allowing a wide variety of vegetation to flourish throughout the island.

Urban districts contain numerous public gardens, while the southern countryside supports large-scale agriculture.

---

## Common Trees

Orange Tree

The island's symbolic tree.

Large orchards surround the southern countryside.

Produces sweet citrus exported across East Blue.

---

Oak

Used extensively in furniture making and ship construction.

---

Pine

Common throughout western hills.

Provides timber and resin.

---

Maple

Frequently planted along roads and public parks.

---

Willow

Found beside rivers and irrigation canals.

---

## Agricultural Crops

Major Crops

- Wheat
- Rice

- Potatoes

- Cabbage
- Carrots
- Onions

Fruit

- Oranges

- Pears

---

## Medicinal Plants

Golden Mint

Used against fever.

---

White Sage

Common ingredient in herbal medicine.

---

Blue Clover

Promotes wound recovery.

---

Sea Lavender

Collected near the coast.

Produces fragrant medicinal oil.

---

## Rare Plants

Sun Blossom

Blooms only during midsummer.

Highly valued by herbalists.

---

Silver Orchid

Rare flower found in western hills.

Protected by local law.

# SEA LIFE

The waters surrounding Orange Town support commercial fishing.

Common Species

- Sardines
- Snapper
- Mackerel
- Swordfish
- Squid
- Octopus
- Lobster
- Shrimp

Marine Mammals

- Sea Turtles

Large sharks occasionally appear offshore.

Sea Kings are extremely rare.

# NATURAL HAZARDS

Although generally peaceful, Orange Town experiences several natural dangers.

Common Hazards

- Coastal Storms
- Harbor Flooding
- Forest Fires
- Landslides in Western Hills
- River Flooding
- Strong Seasonal Winds

Emergency systems are well developed.

# LOCAL RUMORS

Game Masters may introduce these rumors naturally during conversations.

1. A merchant vessel recently arrived carrying cargo that no customs officer was allowed to inspect.

2. Someone has been purchasing enormous quantities of steel without revealing their identity.

3. A forgotten tunnel supposedly connects the old warehouse district to the harbor.

4. Several counterfeit Belly coins have appeared throughout local markets.

5. Dock workers claim strange lights can occasionally be seen beneath the harbor after midnight.

6. A wealthy collector is secretly searching for an ancient navigation log hidden somewhere on the island.

7. An abandoned warehouse has recently become active again despite officially being condemned.

8. Travelers report that a mysterious merchant appears only during heavy rain before disappearing without leaving records.

9. Local fishermen claim something massive has begun living beneath the western cliffs.

10. A retired navigator insists he discovered a forgotten sea route leading toward an unknown island.

---

# RANDOM ENCOUNTERS

Roll 1D20 while exploring Orange Town.

| Roll | Encounter |
|------|-----------|
|1|A merchant asks the party to guard valuable cargo.|
|2|Street performers gather a large crowd in the town square.|
|3|Marine patrol requests identification from travelers.|
|4|A child claims they found a treasure map.|
|5|A runaway cart loaded with fruit speeds downhill.|
|6|A pickpocket attempts to steal a coin purse.|
|7|Two merchants loudly argue over ownership of cargo.|
|8|Heavy rain floods portions of the market district.|
|9|A traveling doctor offers free medical treatment.|
|10|Workers unload a rare foreign vessel.|
|11|A warehouse catches fire unexpectedly.|
|12|A sailor offers information in exchange for food.|
|13|An old navigator asks for help translating an ancient chart.|
|14|A public auction begins in the central plaza.|
|15|Dock workers discover an unregistered crate floating in the harbor.|
|16|A messenger urgently searches for the town council.|
|17|Several seagulls aggressively steal food from nearby stalls.|
|18|An injured merchant collapses near the docks.|
|19|A famous traveling craftsman opens a temporary workshop.|
|20|A suspicious stranger quietly follows the party through the market.|

# ADVENTURE HOOKS

## Missing Merchant Fleet

Three merchant vessels disappear while traveling between Orange Town and Loguetown.

No wreckage has been discovered.

The Merchant Guild hires independent adventurers before trade routes become unsafe.

---

## Counterfeit Belly

Large quantities of counterfeit Belly begin circulating throughout the city.

Tracing their origin may uncover an organized criminal network operating beneath the harbor.

---

## Warehouse 17

An abandoned warehouse suddenly shows signs of activity.

Workers hear machinery every night despite the building officially being empty.

---

## Harbor Sabotage

Several ships suffer identical structural failures shortly after leaving port.

Someone may be sabotaging vessels before departure.

---

## The Forgotten Ledger

A former Guild accountant vanishes after claiming to possess records exposing decades of corruption.

Several organizations race to recover the missing ledger first.

---

## Festival of Commerce

During the annual Grand Trade Festival, priceless merchandise from across East Blue is displayed publicly.

Perfect opportunity for thieves...

...or heroes.

---

Ruins

Natural Cave System

# HIDDEN LOCATIONS

## Forgotten Customs Office

A former customs building abandoned decades ago.

Several secret rooms remain undiscovered.

---

## Merchant Vault

An underground treasury constructed beneath the Banking District.

Few citizens know its exact location.

---

## Smuggler Dock

A concealed harbor accessible only during specific tides.

Ideal for illegal cargo transfers.

---

## The Old Observatory

Hidden atop the western hills.

Contains remarkably accurate star charts created long before modern navigation.

---

# SECRETS

These details should remain hidden until discovered naturally.

Secret 1

One respected merchant secretly finances multiple criminal organizations while publicly supporting law enforcement.

---

Secret 2

The Harbor Authority possesses confidential sea charts unavailable to ordinary navigators.

---

Secret 3

Several abandoned warehouses connect through forgotten underground tunnels beneath the city.

---

Secret 4

A shipment believed lost decades ago still lies somewhere beneath Orange Harbor.

Its cargo could dramatically change local commerce if recovered.

---

Secret 5

Certain influential council members quietly manipulate market prices using privileged shipping information.

# END OF PART 5
---

# GM NOTES

## Recommended Campaign Length

5–12 Sessions

Orange Town functions best as a recurring hub that players revisit throughout an East Blue campaign.

Unlike remote islands, Orange Town should evolve over time as trade, politics, and player actions reshape the city.

---

## Recommended Player Level

Beginning Characters

Level 1–12

Orange Town is designed as one of the first major cities players encounter.

It offers opportunities for:

- Equipment Upgrades
- Crew Recruitment
- Trading
- Information Gathering
- Side Quests
- Political Intrigue

---

## Core Themes

- Commerce
- Civilization
- Opportunity
- Corruption
- Investigation
- Maritime Trade
- Social Interaction

Unlike isolated survival-focused islands, Orange Town emphasizes roleplaying and diplomacy.

---

# WORLD IMPACT

Player actions may permanently affect Orange Town.

Possible Changes

Merchant Prosperity

★★★★★ → ★☆☆☆☆

Crime Rate

Increase or Decrease

Marine Presence

Expanded or Reduced

Harbor Traffic

Busier or Declines

Food Prices

Rise or Fall

Population Growth

Migration increases or decreases.

Political Stability

Town Council elections may produce different leaders.

Public Opinion

Citizens remember major events for years.

---

# REPUTATION EFFECTS

Friendly Reputation

Benefits

- Merchant Discounts
- Better Inn Prices
- Easier Information Gathering
- Guild Invitations
- Exclusive Trade Contracts

---

Neutral Reputation

Citizens treat players normally.

Prices remain standard.

---

Negative Reputation

Consequences

- Increased Guard Attention
- Higher Prices
- Merchants Refuse Service
- Guild Restrictions
- Difficulty Finding Work

---

Wanted Criminal

Effects

- Marine Pursuit
- Harbor Access Restricted
- Bounty Hunters Appear
- Shops Close Their Doors
- Secret Criminal Contacts Become Available

---

# DAILY LIFE

Morning

Fishing boats depart.

Markets prepare for business.

Merchant ships arrive.

---

Afternoon

Warehouses become crowded.

Trade reaches peak activity.

Restaurants fill with travelers.

---

Evening

Street food vendors open.

Entertainment districts become lively.

Ships prepare for departure.

---

Night

Harbor traffic decreases.

Marine patrols increase.

Black-market activity quietly begins.

---

# CONNECTIONS

Regular Shipping Routes

- Dawn Island
- Ember Reef
- Shells Town
- Syrup Village
- Baratie
- Loguetown

Average Merchant Travel Time

1–4 Days

depending on destination.

---

# DESIGN NOTES

Orange Town should always feel alive.

Every visit should present different opportunities.

Merchants should remember previous transactions.

NPC schedules should change according to

- Time of Day
- Weather
- Economy
- Festivals
- Crime Level
- Player Reputation

The city should never feel static.

Trade prices fluctuate naturally.

Warehouses fill and empty.

Ships arrive and depart.

Citizens react to news from neighboring islands.

The world continues moving whether or not the players are present.

---

# SILVER MIST ISLAND

# ==================================================

Sea: East Blue Classification: Canon Island World Type: One Piece
Parallel World

------------------------------------------------------------------------

# OVERVIEW

Silver Mist Island is a medium-sized island in East Blue surrounded by
dense sea fog throughout most of the year. Its isolated environment has
shaped a self-reliant fishing community and made the island a difficult
destination for pirates and merchants alike.

------------------------------------------------------------------------

# GEOGRAPHY

Island Size

Medium

Approximate Diameter

72 km

Highest Elevation

Mist Peak

Terrain

-   Hills
-   Wetlands
-   Rocky Coast

-   Seaweed
-   Hardwood

# GEKKO ATOLL

# ==================================================

Sea: East Blue Classification: Canon Island World Type: One Piece
Parallel World

------------------------------------------------------------------------

# OVERVIEW

Gekko Atoll is a ring-shaped coral atoll in East Blue. Calm lagoons lie
inside the reef while the outer waters are notorious for hidden coral
formations that can wreck careless ships. The island supports small
coastal communities that depend on fishing, pearl diving, and coral
harvesting.

------------------------------------------------------------------------

Small

Approximate Diameter

48 km

Terrain

# BARATIE

# ==================================================

Sea: East Blue Classification: Canon Sea Restaurant World Type: One
Piece Parallel World

------------------------------------------------------------------------

# OVERVIEW

Baratie is a floating sea restaurant operating in East Blue. Built upon
a massive ship, it welcomes travelers, merchants, Marines, bounty
hunters, and pirates alike. Neutrality and hospitality are valued above
politics, though violence against guests is met with swift response.

------------------------------------------------------------------------

# STRUCTURE

Main Sections

-   Grand Dining Hall
-   Guest Cabins
-   Central Kitchen
-   Supply Warehouse
-   Observation Deck
-   Crew Quarters
-   Dry Storage
-   Docking Platforms

-   Restaurant
-   Lodging
-   Ship Resupply
-   Fresh Water
-   Emergency Repairs

120--250

------------------------------------------------------------------------

Approximately 140

Most are chefs, servers, suppliers, and sailors.

by the World Government.

# ARLONG PARK

# ==================================================

Sea: East Blue Classification: Canon Location World Type: One Piece
Parallel World

------------------------------------------------------------------------

# OVERVIEW

Arlong Park was once the headquarters of the Arlong Pirates. In the
Parallel World, the site has been reclaimed after the crew's fall. The
remaining structures stand as a reminder of the island's troubled past,
while nearby communities work to rebuild the area into a peaceful
coastal district.

------------------------------------------------------------------------

# GEOGRAPHY
